\t\t}\n223: \t}\n224: \n225: \treturn nil\n226: }\n227: \n228: // postApplyHook calls the post-Apply hook\n229: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) postApplyHook(ctx EvalContext, state deposedKey states.DeposedKey) error {\n528: \tchanges := ctx.Changes()\n529: \n530: \tif change == nil {\n531: \t\t// Caller sets nil to indicate that we need to remove a change from\n532: \t\t// the a refresh for a resource\n580: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) refresh(ctx EvalContext, deposedKey states.DeposedKey, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject) (*states.ResourceInstanceObject, \t\treturn ret, diags\n715: \t}\n716: \n717: \t// Mark the value if necessary\n718: \tif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n719: \t\tret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n720: \t}\n721: \n722: \treturn ret, diags\n723: }\n724: \n725: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) plan(\n726: \tctx EvalContext,\n727: \tplannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange,\n728: \tcurrentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject,\n729: \tcreateBeforeDestroy bool,\n730: \tforceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance,\n731: ) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, treating it as a\n1188: \t// create.\n1189: \tif action == plans.Create && !priorValTainted.IsNull() {\n1190: \t\tif createBeforeDestroy {\n1191: \t\t\taction = plans.CreateThenDelete\n1192: \t\t} else {\n1193: \t\t\taction = plans.DeleteThenCreate\n1194: \t\t}\n1195: \t\tpriorVal = priorValTainted\n1196: \t\tactionReason = plans.ResourceInstanceReplaceBecauseTainted\n1197: \t}\n1198: \n1199: \t// If we plan to write or delete sensitive paths from state,\n1200: \t// this is an Update action.\n1201: \t//\n1202: \t// We need to filter out any marks which may not apply to the new planned\n1203: \t// value before comparison. The one case where a provider is allowed to\n1204: \t// return a different value from the configuration is when a config change\n1205: \t// is not functionally significant and the prior state can be returned. If a\n1206: \t// new mark was also discarded from that config change, it needs to be\n1207: \t// ignored here to prevent an errant update action.\n1208: \tif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n1209: \t\taction = plans.Update\n1210: \t}\n1211: \n1212: \t// As a special case, if we have a previous diff (presumably from the plan\n1213: \t// phases, whereas we're now in the apply phase) and it was for a replace,\n1214: \t// we've already deleted the original object from state by the time we\n1215: \t// get here and so we would've ended up with a _create_ action this time,\n1216: \t// which we now need to paper over to get a result consistent with what\n1217: \t// we originally intended.\n1218: \tif plannedChange != nil {\n1219: \t\tprevChange := *plannedChange\n1220: \t\tif prevChange.Action.IsReplace() && action == plans.Create {\n1221: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] plan: %s treating Create change as %s change to match with earlier plan\", n.Addr, prevChange.Action)\n1222: \t\t\taction = prevChange.Action\n1223: \t\t\tpriorVal = prevChange.Before\n1224: \t\t}\n1225: \t}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Call post-refresh hook\n1228: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n1229: \t\treturn h.PostDiff(n.Addr, addrs.NotDeposed, action, priorVal, plannedNewVal)\n1230: \t}))\n1231: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1232: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1233: \t}\n1234: \n1235: \t// Update our return plan\n1236: \tplan := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n1237: \t\tAddr:         n.Addr,\n1238: \t\tPrevRunAddr:  n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n1239: \t\tPrivate:      plannedPrivate,\n1240: \t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n1241: \t\tChange: plans.Change{\n1242: \t\t\tAction: action,\n1243: \t\t\tBefore: priorVal,\n1244: \t\t\t// Pass the marked planned value through in our change\n1245: \t\t\t// to propogate through evaluation.\n1246: \t\t\t// Marks will be removed when encoding.\n1247: \t\t\tAfter:           plannedNewVal,\n1248: \t\t\tGeneratedConfig: n.generatedConfigHCL,\n1249: \t\t},\n1250: \t\tActionReason:    actionReason,\n1251: \t\tRequiredReplace: reqRep,\n1252: \t}\n1253: \n1254: \t// Update our return state\n1255: \tstate := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1256: \t\t// We use the special \"planned\" status here to note that this\n1257: \t\t// object's value is not yet complete. Objects with this status\n1258: \t\t// cannot be used during expression evaluation, so the caller\n1259: \t\t// must _also_ record the returned change in the active plan,\n1260: \t\t// which the expression evaluator will use in preference to this\n1261: \t\t// incomplete value recorded in the state.\n1262: \t\tStatus:  states.ObjectPlanned,\n1263: \t\tValue:   plannedNewVal,\n1264: \t\tPrivate: plannedPrivate,\n1265: \t}\n1266: \n1267: \treturn plan, state, keyData, diags\n1268: }\n1269: \n1270: func (n *NodeAbstractResource) processIgnoreChanges(prior, config cty.Value, schema *configschema.Block) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1271: \t// ignore_changes only applies when an object already exists, since we\n1272: \t// can't ignore changes to a thing we've not created yet.\n1273: \tif prior.IsNull() {\n1274: \t\treturn config, nil\n1275: \t}\n1276: \n1277: \tignoreChanges := traversalsToPaths(n.Config.Managed.IgnoreChanges)\n1278: \tignoreAll := n.Config.Managed.IgnoreAllChanges\n1279: \n1280: \tif len(ignoreChanges) == 0 && !ignoreAll {\n1281: \t\treturn config, nil\n1282: \t}\n1283: \n1284: \tif ignoreAll {\n1285: \t\t// Legacy providers need up to clean up their invalid plans and ensure\n1286: \t\t// no changes are passed though, but that also means making an invalid\n1287: \t\t// config with computed values. In that case we just don't supply a\n1288: \t\t// schema and return the prior val directly.\n1289: \t\tif schema == nil {\n1290: \t\t\treturn prior, nil\n1291: \t\t}\n1292: \n1293: \t\t// If we are trying to ignore all attribute changes, we must filter\n1294: \t\t// computed attributes out from the prior state to avoid sending them\n1295: \t\t// to the provider as if they were included in the configuration.\n1296: \t\tret, _ := cty.Transform(prior, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n1297: \t\t\tattr := schema.AttributeByPath(path)\n1298: \t\t\tif attr != nil && attr.Computed && !attr.Optional {\n1299: \t\t\t\treturn cty.NullVal(v.Type()), nil\n1300: \t\t\t}\n1301: \n1302: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1303: \t\t})\n1304: \n1305: \t\treturn ret, nil\n1306: \t}\n1307: \n1308: \tif prior.IsNull() || config.IsNull() {\n1309: \t\t// Ignore changes doesn't apply when we're creating for the first time.\n1310: \t\t// Proposed should never be null here, but if it is then we'll just let it be.\n1311: \t\treturn config, nil\n1312: \t}\n1313: \n1314: \tret, diags := processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config, ignoreChanges)\n1315: \n1316: \treturn ret, diags\n1317: }\n1318: \n1319: // Convert the hcl.Traversal values we get form the configuration to the\n1320: // cty.Path values we need to operate on the cty.Values\n1321: func traversalsToPaths(traversals []hcl.Traversal) []cty.Path {\n1322: \tpaths := make([]cty.Path, len(traversals))\n1323: \tfor i, traversal := range traversals {\n1324: \t\tpath := traversalToPath(traversal)\n1325: \t\tpaths[i] = path\n1326: \t}\n1327: \treturn paths\n1328: }\n1329: \n1330: func traversalToPath(traversal hcl.Traversal) cty.Path {\n1331: \tpath := make(cty.Path, len(traversal))\n1332: \tfor si, step := range traversal {\n1333: \t\tswitch ts := step.(type) {\n1334: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseRoot:\n1335: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1336: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1337: \t\t\t}\n1338: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseAttr:\n1339: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1340: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1341: \t\t\t}\n1342: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseIndex:\n1343: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.IndexStep{\n1344: \t\t\t\tKey: ts.Key,\n1345: \t\t\t}\n1346: \t\tdefault:\n1347: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unsupported traversal step %#v\", step))\n1348: \t\t}\n1349: \t}\n1350: \treturn path\n1351: }\n1352: \n1353: func processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config cty.Value, ignoreChangesPath []cty.Path) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1354: \ttype ignoreChange struct {\n1355: \t\t// Path is the full path, minus any trailing map index\n1356: \t\tpath cty.Path\n1357: \t\t// Value is the value we are to retain at the above path. If there is a\n1358: \t\t// key value, this must be a map and the desired value will be at the\n1359: \t\t// key index.\n1360: \t\tvalue cty.Value\n1361: \t\t// Key is the index key if the ignored path ends in a map index.\n1362: \t\tkey cty.Value\n1363: \t}\n1364: \tvar ignoredValues []ignoreChange\n1365: \n1366: \t// Find the actual changes first and store them in the ignoreChange struct.\n1367: \t// If the change was to a map value, and the key doesn't exist in the\n1368: \t// config, it would never be visited in the transform walk.\n1369: \tfor _, icPath := range ignoreChangesPath {\n1370: \t\tkey := cty.NullVal(cty.String)\n1371: \t\t// check for a map index, since maps are the only structure where we\n1372: \t\t// could have invalid path steps.\n1373: \t\tlast, ok := icPath[len(icPath)-1].(cty.IndexStep)\n1374: \t\tif ok {\n1375: \t\t\tif last.Key.Type() == cty.String {\n1376: \t\t\t\ticPath = icPath[:len(icPath)-1]\n1377: \t\t\t\tkey = last.Key\n1378: \t\t\t}\n1379: \t\t}\n1380: \n1381: \t\t// The structure should have been validated already, and we already\n1382: \t\t// trimmed the trailing map index. Any other intermediate index error\n1383: \t\t// means we wouldn't be able to apply the value below, so no need to\n1384: \t\t// record this.\n1385: \t\tp, err := icPath.Apply(prior)\n1386: \t\tif err != nil {\n1387: \t\t\tcontinue\n1388: \t\t}\n1389: \t\tc, err := icPath.Apply(config)\n1390: \t\tif err != nil {\n1391: \t\t\tcontinue\n1392: \t\t}\n1393: \n1394: \t\t// If this is a map, it is checking the entire map value for equality\n1395: \t\t// rather than the individual key. This means that the change is stored\n1396: \t\t// here even if our ignored key doesn't change. That is OK since it\n1397: \t\t// won't cause any changes in the transformation, but allows us to skip\n1398: \t\t// breaking up the maps and checking for key existence here too.\n1399: \t\tif !p.RawEquals(c) {\n1400: \t\t\t// there a change to ignore at this path, store the prior value\n1401: \t\t\tignoredValues = append(ignoredValues, ignoreChange{icPath, p, key})\n1402: \t\t}\n1403: \t}\n1404: \n1405: \tif len(ignoredValues) == 0 {\n1406: \t\treturn config, nil\n1407: \t}\n1408: \n1409: \tret, _ := cty.Transform(config, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n1410: \t\t// Easy path for when we are only matching the entire value. The only\n1411: \t\t// values we break up for inspection are maps.\n1412: \t\tif !v.Type().IsMapType() {\n1413: \t\t\tfor _, ignored := range ignoredValues {\n1414: \t\t\t\tif path.Equals(ignored.path) {\n1415: \t\t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1416: \t\t\t\t}\n1417: \t\t\t}\n1418: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1419: \t\t}\n1420: \t\t// We now know this must be a map, so we need to accumulate the values\n1421: \t\t// key-by-key.\n1422: \n1423: \t\tif !v.IsNull() && !v.IsKnown() {\n1424: \t\t\t// since v is not known, we cannot ignore individual keys\n1425: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1426: \t\t}\n1427: \n1428: \t\t// The map values will remain as cty values, so we only need to store\n1429: \t\t// the marks from the outer map itself\n1430: \t\tv, vMarks := v.Unmark()\n1431: \n1432: \t\t// The configMap is the current configuration value, which we will\n1433: \t\t// mutate based on the ignored paths and the prior map value.\n1434: \t\tvar configMap map[string]cty.Value\n1435: \t\tswitch {\n1436: \t\tcase v.IsNull() || v.LengthInt() == 0:\n1437: \t\t\tconfigMap = map[string]cty.Value{}\n1438: \t\tdefault:\n1439: \t\t\tconfigMap = v.AsValueMap()\n1440: \t\t}\n1441: \n1442: \t\tfor _, ignored := range ignoredValues {\n1443: \t\t\tif !path.Equals(ignored.path) {\n1444: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1445: \t\t\t}\n1446: \n1447: \t\t\tif ignored.key.IsNull() {\n1448: \t\t\t\t// The map address is confirmed to match at this point,\n1449: \t\t\t\t// so if there is no key, we want the entire map and can\n1450: \t\t\t\t// stop accumulating values.\n1451: \t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1452: \t\t\t}\n1453: \t\t\t// Now we know we are ignoring a specific index of this map, so get\n1454: \t\t\t// the config map and modify, add, or remove the desired key.\n1455: \n1456: \t\t\t// We also need to create a prior map, so we can check for\n1457: \t\t\t// existence while getting the value, because Value.Index will\n1458: \t\t\t// return null for a key with a null value and for a non-existent\n1459: \t\t\t// key.\n1460: \t\t\tvar priorMap map[string]cty.Value\n1461: \n1462: \t\t\t// We need to drop the marks from the ignored map for handling. We\n1463: \t\t\t// don't need to store these, as we now know the ignored value is\n1464: \t\t\t// only within the map, not the map itself.\n1465: \t\t\tignoredVal, _ := ignored.value.Unmark()\n1466: \n1467: \t\t\tswitch {\n1468: \t\t\tcase ignored.value.IsNull() || ignoredVal.LengthInt() == 0:\n1469: \t\t\t\tpriorMap = map[string]cty.Value{}\n1470: \t\t\tdefault:\n1471: \t\t\t\tpriorMap = ignoredVal.AsValueMap()\n1472: \t\t\t}\n1473: \n1474: \t\t\tkey := ignored.key.AsString()\n1475: \t\t\tpriorElem, keep := priorMap[key]\n1476: \n1477: \t\t\tswitch {\n1478: \t\t\tcase !keep:\n1479: \t\t\t\t// this didn't exist in the old map value, so we're keeping the\n1480: \t\t\t\t// \"absence\" of the key by removing it from the config\n1481: \t\t\t\tdelete(configMap, key)\n1482: \t\t\tdefault:\n1483: \t\t\t\tconfigMap[key] = priorElem\n1484: \t\t\t}\n1485: \t\t}\n1486: \n1487: \t\tvar newVal cty.Value\n1488: \t\tswitch {\n1489: \t\tcase len(configMap) > 0:\n1490: \t\t\tnewVal = cty.MapVal(configMap)\n1491: \t\tcase v.IsNull():\n1492: \t\t\t// if the config value was null, and no values remain in the map,\n1493: \t\t\t// reset the value to null.\n1494: \t\t\tnewVal = v\n1495: \t\tdefault:\n1496: \t\t\tnewVal = cty.MapValEmpty(v.Type().ElementType())\n1497: \t\t}\n1498: \n1499: \t\tif len(vMarks) > 0 {\n1500: \t\t\tnewVal = newVal.WithMarks(vMarks)\n1501: \t\t}\n1502: \n1503: \t\treturn newVal, nil\n1504: \t})\n1505: \treturn ret, nil\n1506: }\n1507: \n1508: // readDataSource handles everything needed to call ReadDataSource on the provider.\n1509: // A previously evaluated configVal can be passed in, or a new one is generated\n1510: // from the resource configuration.\n1511: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) readDataSource(ctx EvalContext, \t\t\t// if the provider doesn't support this feature, throw an error\n1656: \t\t\tif providerSchema.ProviderMeta.Block == nil {\n1657: \t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n1658: fmt.Sprintf(\"The resource %s belongs to a provider that doesn't support provider_meta blocks\", n.Addr.Resource),\n1661: \t\t\t\t\tSubject:  &m.ProviderRange,\n1662: \t\t\t\t})\n1663: \t\t\t} else {\n1664: \t\t\t\tvar configDiags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1665: \t\t\t\tmetaConfigVal, _, configDiags = ctx.EvaluateBlock(m.Config, providerSchema.ProviderMeta.Block, nil, EvalDataForNoInstanceKey)\n1666: \t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(configDiags)\n1667: \t\t\t}\n1668: \t\t}\n1669: \t}\n1670: \treturn metaConfigVal, diags\n1671: }\n1672: \n1673: // planDataSource deals with the main part of the data resource lifecycle:\n1674: // either actually reading from the data source or generating a plan to do so.\n1675: //\n1676: // currentState is the current state for the data source, and the new state is\n1677: // returned. While data sources are read-only, we need to start with the prior\n1678: // state to determine if we have a change or not.  If we needed to read a new\n1679: // value, but it still matches the previous state, then we can record a NoNop\n1680: // change. If the states don't match then we record a Read change so that the\n1681: // new value is applied to the state.\n1682: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) planDataSource(ctx EvalContext, checkRuleSeverity tfdiags.Severity, skipPlanChanges bool) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1683: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1684: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n1685: \tvar configVal cty.Value\n1686: \n1687: \t_, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n1688: \tif err != nil {\n1689: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags.Append(err)\n1690: \t}\n1691: \n1692: \tconfig := *n.Config\n1693: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(n.Addr.ContainingResource().Resource)\n1694: \tif schema == nil {\n1695: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n1696: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"provider %q does not support data source %q\", n.ResolvedProvider, n.Addr.ContainingResource().Resource.Type))\n1697: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1698: \t}\n1699: \n1700: \tobjTy := schema.ImpliedType()\n1701: \tpriorVal := cty.NullVal(objTy)\n1702: \n1703: \tforEach, _ := evaluateForEachExpression(config.ForEach, ctx)\n1704: \tkeyData = EvalDataForInstanceKey(n.ResourceInstanceAddr().Resource.Key, forEach)\n1705: \n1706: \tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\n1707: \t\taddrs.ResourcePrecondition,\n1708: \t\tn.Config.Preconditions,\n1709: \t\tctx, n.Addr, keyData,\n1710: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity,\n1711: \t)\n1712: \tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\n1713: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1714: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags // failed preconditions prevent further evaluation\n1715: \t}\n1716: \n1717: \tvar configDiags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1718: \tconfigVal, _, configDiags = ctx.EvaluateBlock(config.Config, schema, nil, keyData)\n1719: \tdiags = diags.Append(configDiags)\n1720: \tif configDiags.HasErrors() {\n1721: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1722: \t}\n1723: \n1724: \tcheck, nested := n.nestedInCheckBlock()\n1725: \tif nested {\n1726: \t\t// Going forward from this point, the only reason we will fail is\n1727: \t\t// that the data source fails to load its data. Normally, this would\n1728: \t\t// cancel the entire plan and this error message would bubble its way\n1729: \t\t// back up to the user.\n1730: \t\t//\n1731: \t\t// But, if we are in a check block then we don't want this data block to\n1732: \t\t// cause the plan to fail. We also need to report a status on the data\n1733: \t\t// block so the check processing later on knows whether to attempt to\n1734: \t\t// process the checks. Either we'll report the data block as failed\n1735: \t\t// if/when we load the data block later, or we want to report it as a\n1736: \t\t// success overall.\n1737: \t\t//\n1738: \t\t// Therefore, we create a deferred function here that will check if the\n1739: \t\t// status for the check has been updated yet, and if not we will set it\n1740: \t\t// to be StatusPass. The rest of this function will only update the\n1741: \t\t// status if it should be StatusFail.\n1742: \t\tdefer func() {\n1743: \t\t\tstatus := ctx.Checks().ObjectCheckStatus(check.Addr().Absolute(n.Addr.Module))\n1744: \t\t\tif status == checks.StatusUnknown {\n1745: \t\t\t\tctx.Checks().ReportCheckResult(check.Addr().Absolute(n.Addr.Module), addrs.CheckDataResource, 0, checks.StatusPass)\n1746: \t\t\t}\n1747: \t\t}()\n1748: \t}\n1749: \n1750: \tconfigKnown := configVal.IsWhollyKnown()\n1751: \tdepsPending := n.dependenciesHavePendingChanges(ctx)\n1752: \t// If our configuration contains any unknown values, or we depend on any\n1753: \t// unknown values then we must defer the read to the apply phase by\n1754: \t// producing a \"Read\" change for this resource, and a placeholder value for\n1755: \t// it in the state.\n1756: \tif depsPending || !configKnown {\n1757: \t\t// We can't plan any changes if we're only refreshing, so the only\n1758: \t\t// value we can set here is whatever was in state previously.\n1759: \t\tif skipPlanChanges {\n1760: \t\t\tplannedNewState := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1761: \t\t\t\tValue:  priorVal,\n1762: \t\t\t\tStatus: states.ObjectReady,\n1763: \t\t\t}\n1764: \n1765: \t\t\treturn nil, plannedNewState, keyData, diags\n1766: \t\t}\n1767: \n1768: \t\tvar reason plans.ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason\n1769: \t\tswitch {\n1770: \t\tcase !configKnown:\n1771: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] planDataSource: %s configuration not fully known yet, so deferring to apply phase\", n.Addr)\n1772: \t\t\treason = plans.ResourceInstanceReadBecauseConfigUnknown\n1773: \t\tcase depsPending:\n1774: \t\t\t// NOTE: depsPending can be true at the same time as configKnown\n1775: \t\t\t// is false; configKnown takes precedence because it's more\n1776: \t\t\t// specific.\n1777: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] planDataSource: %s configuration is fully known, at least one dependency has changes pending\", n.Addr)\n1778: \t\t\treason = plans.ResourceInstanceReadBecauseDependencyPending\n1779: \t\t}\n1780: \n1781: \t\tunmarkedConfigVal, configMarkPaths := configVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n1782: \t\tproposedNewVal := objchange.PlannedDataResourceObject(schema, unmarkedConfigVal)\n1783: \t\tproposedNewVal = proposedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(configMarkPaths)\n1784: \n1785: \t\t// Apply detects that the data source will need to be read by the After\n1786: \t\t// value containing unknowns from PlanDataResourceObject.\n1787: \t\tplannedChange := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n1788: \t\t\tAddr:         n.Addr,\n1789: \t\t\tPrevRunAddr:  n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n1790: \t\t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n1791: \t\t\tChange: plans.Change{\n1792: \t\t\t\tAction: plans.Read,\n1793: \t\t\t\tBefore: priorVal,\n1794: \t\t\t\tAfter:  proposedNewVal,\n1795: \t\t\t},\n1796: \t\t\tActionReason: reason,\n1797: \t\t}\n1798: \n1799: \t\tplannedNewState := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1800: \t\t\tValue: addrs.NotDeposed, plans.Read, priorVal, proposedNewVal)\n1806: \t\t}))\n1807: \n1808: \t\treturn plannedChange, plannedNewState, keyData, diags\n1809: \t}\n1810: \n1811: \t// We have a complete configuration with no dependencies to wait on, so we\n1812: \t// can read the data source into the state.\n1813: \tnewVal, readDiags := n.readDataSource(ctx, configVal)\n1814: \n1815: \t// Now we've *plans.ResourceInstanceChange\n1819: \tvar plannedNewState *states.ResourceInstanceObject\n1820: \n1821: \t// If we are a nested block, then we want to create a plannedChange that\n1822: \t// tells \t// disguise that for a nested block. So,\n1835: \t\t// if we encountered an error we'll tidy up newVal so it makes sense\n1836: \t\t// and handle the error. We'll also create the plannedChange if\n1837: \t\t// appropriate.\n1838: \n1839: \t\tif readDiags.HasErrors() {\n1840: \t\t\t// If we had errors, then we can cover that up by marking the new\n1841: \t\t\t// state as unknown.\n1842: \t\t\tunmarkedConfigVal, configMarkPaths := configVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n1843: \t\t\tnewVal = objchange.PlannedDataResourceObject(schema, unmarkedConfigVal)\n1844: \t\t\tnewVal = newVal.MarkWithPaths(configMarkPaths)\n1845: \n1846: \t\t\t// We still want to report the check as failed even if we are still\n1847: \t\t\t// letting it run again during the apply stage.\n1848: \t\t\tctx.Checks().ReportCheckFailure(addr, addrs.CheckDataResource, 0, readDiags.Err().Error())\n1849: \t\t}\n1850: \n1851: \t\t// Any warning or error diagnostics we'll wrap with some special checks\n1852: \t\t// diagnostics. This is so we can identify them later, and so they'll\n1853: \t\t// only report as warnings.\n1854: \t\treadDiags = tfdiags.OverrideAll(readDiags, tfdiags.Warning, func() tfdiags.DiagnosticExtraWrapper {\n1855: \t\t\treturn &addrs.CheckRuleDiagnosticExtra{\n1856: \t\t\t\tCheckRule: addrs.NewCheckRule(addr, addrs.CheckDataResource, 0),\n1857: \t\t\t}\n1858: \t\t})\n1859: \n1860: \t\tif !skipPlanChanges {\n1861: \t\t\t// refreshOnly plans cannot produce planned changes, so we only do\n1862: \t\t\t// this if skipPlanChanges is false.\n1863: \t\t\tplannedChange = &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n1864: \t\t\t\tAddr:         n.Addr,\n1865: \t\t\t\tPrevRunAddr:  n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n1866: \t\t\t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n1867: \t\t\t\tChange: plans.Change{\n1868: \t\t\t\t\tAction: plans.Read,\n1869: \t\t\t\t\tBefore: priorVal,\n1870: \t\t\t\t\tAfter:  newVal,\n1871: \t\t\t\t},\n1872: \t\t\t\tActionReason: plans.ResourceInstanceReadBecauseCheckNested,\n1873: \t\t\t}\n1874: \t\t}\n1875: \t}\n1876: \n1877: \tdiags = diags.Append(readDiags)\n1878: \tif !diags.HasErrors() {\n1879: \t\t// Finally, let's make our new state.\n1880: \t\tplannedNewState = &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1881: \t\t\tValue:  newVal,\n1882: \t\t\tStatus: states.ObjectReady,\n1883: \t\t}\n1884: \t}\n1885: \n1886: \treturn plannedChange, plannedNewState, keyData, diags\n1887: }\n1888: \n1889: // nestedInCheckBlock determines if this resource is nested in a Check config\n1890: // block. If so, this resource will be loaded during both plan and apply\n1891: // operations to make sure the check is always giving the latest information.\n1892: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) nestedInCheckBlock() (*configs.Check, bool) {\n1893: \tif n.Config.Container != nil {\n1894: \t\tcheck, ok := n.Config.Container.(*configs.Check)\n1895: \t\treturn check, ok\n1896: \t}\n1897: \treturn nil, false\n1898: }\n1899: \n1900: // dependenciesHavePendingChanges determines whether any managed resource the\n1901: // receiver depends on has a change pending in the plan, in which case we'd\n1902: // need to override the usual behavior of immediately reading from the data\n1903: // source where possible, and instead defer the read until the apply step.\n1904: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dependenciesHavePendingChanges(ctx EvalContext) bool {\n1905: \tnModInst := n.Addr.Module\n1906: \tnMod := nModInst.Module()\n1907: \n1908: \t// Check and see if any depends_on dependencies have\n1909: \t// changes, since they won't show up as changes in the\n1910: \t// configuration.\n1911: \tchanges := ctx.Changes()\n1912: \n1913: \tdepsToUse := n.dependsOn\n1914: \n1915: \tif n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Mode == addrs.DataResourceMode {\n1916: \t\tif n.Config.HasCustomConditions() {\n1917: \t\t\t// For a data resource with custom conditions we need to look at\n1918: \t\t\t// the full set of resource dependencies -- both direct and\n1919: \t\t\t// indirect -- because an upstream update might be what's needed\n1920: \t\t\t// in order to make a condition pass.\n1921: \t\t\tdepsToUse = n.Dependencies\n1922: \t\t}\n1923: \t}\n1924: \n1925: \tfor _, d := range depsToUse {\n1926: \t\tif d.Resource.Mode == addrs.DataResourceMode {\n1927: \t\t\t// Data sources have no external side effects, so they pose a need\n1928: \t\t\t// to delay this read. If they do have a change planned, it must be\n1929: \t\t\t// because of a dependency on a managed resource, in which case\n1930: \t\t\t// we'll also encounter it in this list of dependencies.\n1931: \t\t\tcontinue\n1932: \t\t}\n1933: \n1934: \t\tfor _, change := range changes.GetChangesForConfigResource(d) {\n1935: \t\t\tchangeModInst := change.Addr.Module\n1936: \t\t\tchangeMod := changeModInst.Module()\n1937: \n1938: \t\t\tif changeMod.Equal(nMod) && !changeModInst.Equal(nModInst) {\n1939: \t\t\t\t// Dependencies are tracked by configuration address, which\n1940: \t\t\t\t// means we may have changes from other instances of parent\n1941: \t\t\t\t// modules. main part of the data resource lifecycle: either\n1956: // actually reading from the data source or generating a plan to do so.\n1957: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyDataSource(ctx EvalContext, planned *plans.ResourceInstanceChange) (*states.ResourceInstanceObject, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1958: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1959: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n1960: \n1961: \t_, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n1962: \tif err != nil {\n1963: \t\treturn nil, keyData, diags.Append(err)\n1964: \t}\n1965: addrs.NewCheckRule(addr, addrs.CheckDataResource, 0),\n2024: \t\t\t\t}\n2025: \t\t\t}))\n2026: \t\t\treturn nil, keyData, diags\n2027: \t\t}\n2028: \n2029: \t\t// Even though we know there are no errors here, we still want to\n2030: \t\t// identify these diags has having been generated from a check block.\n2031: \t\treadDiags = tfdiags.OverrideAll(readDiags, tfdiags.Warning, func() tfdiags.DiagnosticExtraWrapper {\n2032: \t\t\treturn &addrs.CheckRuleDiagnosticExtra{\n2033: \t\t\t\tCheckRule: addrs.NewCheckRule(addr, addrs.CheckDataResource, 0),\n2034: \t\t\t}\n2035: evalApplyProvisioners determines if provisioners need to be run, and if so\n2056: // executes the provisioners for a resource and returns an updated error if\n2057: // provisioning fails.\n2058: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) evalApplyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, createNew bool, when configs.ProvisionerWhen) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2059: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n2060: \n2061: \tif state == nil {\n2062: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalApplyProvisioners: %s has no state, so skipping provisioners\", n.Addr)\n2063: \t\treturn nil\n2064: \t}\n2065: \tif when == configs.ProvisionerWhenCreate && !createNew {\n2066: \t\t// If we're not creating a new resource, then don't run provisioners\n2067: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalApplyProvisioners: %s is not freshly-created, so no provisioning is required\", n.Addr)\n2068: \t\treturn nil\n2069: \t}\n2070: \tif state.Status == states.ObjectTainted {\n2071: \t\t// No point in provisioning an object that is already tainted, since\n2072: \t\t// it's going to get recreated on the next apply anyway.\n2073: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalApplyProvisioners: %s is tainted, so skipping provisioning\", n.Addr)\n2074: \t\treturn nil\n2075: \t}\n2076: \n2077: \tprovs := filterProvisioners(n.Config, when)\n2078: \tif len(provs) == 0 {\n2079: \t\t// We have no provisioners, so don't do anything\n2080: \t\treturn nil\n2081: \t}\n2082: \n2083: \t// Call pre hook\n2084: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n2085: \t\treturn h.PreProvisionInstance(n.Addr, state.Value)\n2086: \t}))\n2087: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n2088: \t\treturn diags\n2089: \t}\n2090: \n2091: \t// If there are no errors, then we append it to our output error\n2092: \t// if we have one, otherwise we just output it.\n2093: \tdiags = diags.Append(n.applyProvisioners(ctx, state, when, provs))\n2094: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n2095: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalApplyProvisioners: %s provisioning failed, but we will continue anyway at the caller's request\", n.Addr)\n2096: \t\treturn diags\n2097: \t}\n2098: \n2099: \t// Call post hook\n2100: \treturn diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n2101: \t\treturn h.PostProvisionInstance(n.Addr, state.Value)\n2102: \t}))\n2103: }\n2104: \n2105: // filterProvisioners filters the provisioners on the resource to only\n2106: // the provisioners specified by the \"when\" option.\n2107: func filterProvisioners(config *configs.Resource, when configs.ProvisionerWhen) []*configs.Provisioner {\n2108: \t// Fast path the zero case\n2109: \tif config == nil || config.Managed == nil {\n2110: \t\treturn nil\n2111: \t}\n2112: \n2113: \tif len(config.Managed.Provisioners) == 0 {\n2114: \t\treturn nil\n2115: \t}\n2116: \n2117: \tresult := make([]*configs.Provisioner, 0, len(config.Managed.Provisioners))\n2118: \tfor _, p := range config.Managed.Provisioners {\n2119: \t\tif p.When == when {\n2120: \t\t\tresult = append(result, p)\n2121: \t\t}\n2122: \t}\n2123: \n2124: \treturn result\n2125: }\n2126: \n2127: // applyProvisioners executes the provisioners for a resource.\n2128: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, when configs.ProvisionerWhen, provs []*configs.Provisioner) Terraform will still save the other known object values in the state.\",\n2536: \t\t\t\t\t\tn.Addr, pathStr,\n2537: \t\t\t\t\t),\n2538: \t\t\t\t))\n2539: \t\t\t}\n2540: \t\t\treturn true, nil\n2541: \t\t})\n2542: \n2543: \t\t// NOTE: This operation can potentially be lossy if there are multiple\n2544: \t\t// elements in a set that differ only by unknown values: after\n2545: \t\t// replacing with null these will be merged together into a single set\n2546: \t\t// element. Since it cannot be moved into the\\n64: \\t// ObjectRead state, a tainted object must be replaced.\\n65: \\tObjectTainted ObjectStatus = 'T'\\n66: \\n67: \\t// ObjectPlanned is a special object status used only for the transient\\n68: \\t// placeholder objects we place into state during the refresh and plan\\n69: \\t// walks to stand in for objects that will be created during apply.\\n70: \\t//\\n71: \\t// Any object of this status must have a corresponding change recorded\\n72: \\t// in the current plan, whose value must then be used in preference to\\n73: \\t// the value stored in state when evaluating expressions. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01WzjNu2MbNtywoKWinVM8cG","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01BxDDTTxaAaZiD3sP5GcatC","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform generates phantom in-place updates for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because sensitivity marks from the provider schema are not persisted in state files. When the value is read back during planning, it lacks these schema-defined marks. The plan comparison at `node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208` detects a difference in sensitivity metadata (even though underlying values are identical), triggering an Update action instead of NoOp. Additionally, the JSON state output shows incomplete `sensitive_values` because the state file only records marks from sensitive variable references, not from the schema.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause is a **fundamental asymmetry in how sensitivity marks are handled between state persistence and runtime evaluation**:\n\n1. **State persistence ignores schema-defined sensitive attributes**: When a resource is encoded to state via `ResourceInstanceObject.Encode()`, only marks present on the value object itself are saved to `AttrSensitivePaths`. These marks come from sensitive variable references (e.g., `var.db_password` marked as sensitive), but NOT from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations.\n\n2. **Runtime evaluation compensates with dynamic mark application**: When values are read for expression evaluation in `GetResource()`, the evaluator re-applies schema-defined marks every time, creating marks that exist only in memory, not in persisted state.\n\n3. **Plan comparison detects the mark difference**: When creating a plan, the code compares refreshed state (which has incomplete marks from state) against the planned state (which also has incomplete marks). However, the comparison logic at line 1208 can detect a sensitivity-only difference and incorrectly convert a NoOp to an Update.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### File: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`\n\n**Refresh Path (lines 578-723)**:\n- Line 625: Provider value is unmarked: `priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()`\n- Line 636-641: Provider's ReadResource() is called, returns response WITHOUT any marks\n- Line 718-720: Only prior marks (from variable references) are re-applied, NOT schema marks:\n  ```go\n  if len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n      ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n  }\n  ```\n\n**Plan Path (lines 725-1268)**:\n- Lines 868-869: Configuration and prior state are unmarked:\n  ```go\n  unmarkedConfigVal, unmarkedPaths := configValIgnored.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n  unmarkedPriorVal, priorPaths := priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n  ```\n- Line 902-910: Provider.PlanResourceChange() receives unmarked values, returns unmarked planned state\n- Line 998-1000: Only configuration marks are re-applied:\n  ```go\n  if len(unmarkedPaths) > 0 {\n      plannedNewVal = plannedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(unmarkedPaths)\n  }\n  ```\n- **Line 1208 - THE PHANTOM DIFF TRIGGER**:\n  ```go\n  if action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n      action = plans.Update\n  }\n  ```\n  This line compares marks from the planned value (configuration marks) with marks from prior state (variable reference marks). If they differ due to schema-defined marks missing from `priorPaths`, it incorrectly triggers an Update.\n\n### File: `internal/states/instance_object.go`\n\n**State Encoding (lines 94-137)**:\n- Line 98: Marks are extracted via UnmarkDeepWithPaths:\n  ```go\n  val, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n  ```\n- Line 131: Only extracted marks are saved to state:\n  ```go\n  AttrSensitivePaths:  pvm,\n  ```\n  This `pvm` (PathValueMarks) contains ONLY marks that were on the value object, which come from sensitive variable references. When the value is read back during planning, it lacks these schema-defined marks. The plan comparison at `node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208` detects a difference in sensitivity metadata (even though underlying values are identical), triggering an Update action instead of NoOp. Additionally, the JSON state output shows incomplete `sensitive_values` because the state file only records marks from sensitive variable references, not from the schema.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause is a **fundamental asymmetry in how sensitivity marks are handled between state persistence and runtime evaluation**:\n\n1. **State persistence ignores schema-defined sensitive attributes**: When a resource is encoded to state via `ResourceInstanceObject.Encode()`, only marks present on the value object itself are saved to `AttrSensitivePaths`. These marks come from sensitive variable references (e.g., `var.db_password` marked as sensitive), but NOT from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations.\n\n2. **Runtime evaluation compensates with dynamic mark application**: When values are read for expression evaluation in `GetResource()`, the evaluator re-applies schema-defined marks every time, creating marks that exist only in memory, not in persisted state.\n\n3. **Plan comparison detects the mark difference**: When creating a plan, the code compares refreshed state (which has incomplete marks from state) against the planned state (which also has incomplete marks). When the value is read back during planning, it lacks these schema-defined marks. The plan comparison at `node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208` detects a difference in sensitivity metadata (even though underlying values are identical), triggering an Update action instead of NoOp. Additionally, the JSON state output shows incomplete `sensitive_values` because the state file only records marks from sensitive variable references, not from the schema.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause is a **fundamental asymmetry in how sensitivity marks are handled between state persistence and runtime evaluation**:\n\n1. **State persistence ignores schema-defined sensitive attributes**: When a resource is encoded to state via `ResourceInstanceObject.Encode()`, only marks present on the value object itself are saved to `AttrSensitivePaths`. These marks come from sensitive variable references (e.g., `var.db_password` marked as sensitive), but NOT from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations.\n\n2. **Runtime evaluation compensates with dynamic mark application**: When values are read for expression evaluation in `GetResource()`, the evaluator re-applies schema-defined marks every time, creating marks that exist only in memory, not in persisted state.\n\n3. **Plan comparison detects the mark difference**: When creating a plan, the code compares refreshed state (which has incomplete marks from state) against the planned state (which also has incomplete marks). However, the comparison logic at line 1208 can detect a sensitivity-only difference and incorrectly convert a NoOp to an Update.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### File: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`\n\n**Refresh Path (lines 578-723)**:\n- Line 625: Provider value is unmarked: `priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()`\n- Line 636-641: Provider's ReadResource() is called, returns response WITHOUT any marks\n- Line 718-720: Only prior marks (from variable references) are re-applied, NOT schema marks:\n  ```go\n  if len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n      ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n  }\n  ```\n\n**Plan Path (lines 725-1268)**:\n- Lines 868-869: Configuration and prior state are unmarked:\n  ```go\n  unmarkedConfigVal, unmarkedPaths := configValIgnored.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n  unmarkedPriorVal, priorPaths := priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n  ```\n- Line 902-910: Provider.PlanResourceChange() receives unmarked values, returns unmarked planned state\n- Line 998-1000: Only configuration marks are re-applied:\n  ```go\n  if len(unmarkedPaths) > 0 {\n      plannedNewVal = plannedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(unmarkedPaths)\n  }\n  ```\n- **Line 1208 - THE PHANTOM DIFF TRIGGER**:\n  ```go\n  if action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n      action = plans.Update\n  }\n  ```\n  This line compares marks from the planned value (configuration marks) with marks from prior state (variable reference marks). If they differ due to schema-defined marks missing from `priorPaths`, it incorrectly triggers an Update.\n\n### File: `internal/states/instance_object.go`\n\n**State Encoding (lines 94-137)**:\n- Line 98: Marks are extracted via UnmarkDeepWithPaths:\n  ```go\n  val, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n  ```\n- Line 131: Only extracted marks are saved to state:\n  ```go\n  AttrSensitivePaths:  pvm,\n  ```\n  This `pvm` (PathValueMarks) contains ONLY marks that were on the value object, which come from sensitive variable references. Schema-defined marks are NOT on the value at this point.\n\n### File: `internal/states/instance_object_src.go`\n\n**State Decoding (lines 77-104)**:\n- Lines 89-91: When decoding, marks are restored from state:\n  ```go\n  if os.AttrSensitivePaths != nil {\n      val = val.MarkWithPaths(os.AttrSensitivePaths)\n  }\n  ```\n  These are ONLY the marks that were in state (variable reference marks), not schema marks.\n\n### File: `internal/terraform/evaluate.go`\n\n**The Compensating Workaround (lines 714-723)**:\n```go\n// If our schema contains sensitive values, mark those as sensitive.\n// Since decoding the instance object can also apply sensitivity marks,\n// we must remove and combine those before remarking to avoid a double-\n// mark error.\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\ninstances[key] = val\n```\n\nThis is the ONLY place in the codebase where schema-defined sensitive marks are re-applied to a value read from state. This happens ONLY during expression evaluation (GetResource), NOT during plan creation.\n\n### File: `internal/command/jsonplan/values.go`\n\n**JSON Output Manifestation (lines 212-235)**:\n```go\n// copy the marked After values so we can use these in marshalSensitiveValues\nmarkedAfter := changeV.After\n\n// ... unmark for JSON output ...\nchangeV.After, _ = changeV.After.UnmarkDeep()\n\n// ... marshal values ...\n\ns := jsonstate.SensitiveAsBool(markedAfter)\nv, err := ctyjson.Marshal(s, s.Type())\nresource.SensitiveValues = v\n```\n\nThe `sensitive_values` in JSON output uses `markedAfter` from the change object. If the change object never had schema marks applied (because it came from the provider response without those marks), the JSON output will be incomplete.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`** - Refresh and plan phases don't apply schema marks\n2. **`internal/states/instance_object.go`** - State encoding loses schema mark information\n3. **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`** - State decoding only restores partial marks\n4. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`** - Compensating workaround applies schema marks only at expression evaluation time\n5. **`internal/terraform/marks.go`** - Utility functions for comparing and filtering marks\n6. **`internal/command/jsonplan/values.go`** - JSON output generation relies on incomplete marks\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Initial state**: Resource with `password` attribute (marked sensitive in provider schema) is successfully applied\n   - Value written to state via `Encode()` → only variable-reference marks are saved\n\n2. **Immediate plan**: `terraform plan` is run with no configuration changes\n   - Resource is refreshed via `refresh()` → provider returns unmarked value\n   - Prior marks from state are re-applied (variable references only)\n   - Planned value from provider is also unmarked\n   - Configuration marks are applied to planned value\n\n3. **Phantom diff detection**: Plan comparison at line 1208\n   - `plannedNewVal` has configuration marks (unmarkedPaths)\n   - `priorVal` has variable-reference marks (priorPaths)\n   - There are two approaches:\n\n**Approach 1 (Preferred): Store schema-defined marks in state**\n- Modify `Encode()` in `instance_object.go` to accept the provider schema and apply `schema.ValueMarks()` before calling `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()`\n- This ensures `AttrSensitivePaths` in state contains ALL sensitive paths (both from references and schema)\n- Eliminates the need for the compensating workaround in `evaluate.go`\n- Makes state the single source of truth for sensitivity information\n- **Impact**: Schema migrations required, potential state file format changes\n\n**Approach 2: Apply schema marks in plan phase**\n- Modify the `plan()` method in `node_resource_abstract_instance.go` to apply schema marks to planned values before comparison (similar to what GetResource does)\n- This makes the plan comparison aware of schema-defined marks without changing state persistence\n- Simpler scope than Approach 1, but maintains the asymmetry\n- **Impact**: Phantom diffs might still occur if state lacks schema marks\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. Compare `AttrSensitivePaths` in state file before and after refresh:\n   - Should have expanded to include schema-defined paths if fixed\n\n2. Verify plan comparison logic:\n   - Add logging to `marksEqual()` call at line 1208 to show what marks are being compared\n\n3. Check JSON output:\n   - `terraform show -json` should include ALL sensitive paths (schema + variable reference)\n   - Compare against provider schema to verify completeness\n\n4.
